<li><i><a class="external text" href="http://isnature.org/Files/Lavoisier1789-Traite_elementaire_de_chimie.htm" rel="nofollow">Traité élémentaire de chimie, présenté dans un ordre nouveau et d'après les découvertes modernes</a></i> (Paris: Chez Cuchet, 1789; Bruxelles: Cultures et Civilisations, 1965) (lit. Elementary Treatise on Chemistry, presented in a new order and alongside modern discoveries) also <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20100109164241/http://www.lavoisier.cnrs.fr/ice/ice_book_detail-fr-text-lavosier-Lavoisier-89-6.html" rel="nofollow">here</a></li>
<li>(with Pierre-Simon Laplace) "<a class="external text" href="http://www.lavoisier.cnrs.fr/ice/ice_page_detail.php?lang=fr&amp;type=text&amp;bdd=lavosier&amp;table=Lavoisier&amp;typeofbookDes=Memoires&amp;bookId=38&amp;pageChapter=M%E9moire%20sur%20la%20chaleur&amp;pageOrder=1&amp;facsimile=off&amp;search=no&amp;num=&amp;nav=1" rel="nofollow">Mémoire sur la chaleur</a>," <i>Mémoires de l'Académie des sciences</i> (1780), pp. 355–408.</li>
<li><i><a class="external text" href="http://www.lavoisier.cnrs.fr/ice/ice_page_detail.php?lang=fr&amp;type=text&amp;bdd=lavosier&amp;table=Lavoisier&amp;typeofbookDes=Memoires&amp;bookId=65&amp;pageChapter=Premier%20m%E9moire%20contenant%20les%20exp%E9riences%20faites%20sur%20la%20chaleur,%20pendant%20l%27hiver%20de%201783%20%E0%201784,%20par%20P.S.%20de%20Laplace%20et%20A.L.%20%20Lavoisier&amp;pageOrder=1&amp;facsimile=off&amp;search=no&amp;num=&amp;nav=1" rel="nofollow">Mémoire contenant les expériences faites sur la chaleur, pendant l'hiver de 1783 à 1784, par P.S. de Laplace &amp; A. K. Lavoisier</a></i> (1792)</li>
<li><i>Mémoires de Physique et de Chimie, de la Société d'Arcueil</i> (1805: posthumous)</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_translation">In translation</span></h3>
<ul><li><i><a class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/essaysphysicala00lavogoog" rel="nofollow">Essays Physical and Chemical</a></i> (London: for Joseph Johnson, 1776; London: Frank Cass and Company Ltd., 1970) translation by Thomas Henry of <i>Opuscules physiques et chimiques</i></li>
<li><i>The Art of Manufacturing Alkaline Salts and Potashes, Published by Order of His Most Christian Majesty, and approved by the Royal Academy of Sciences</i> (1784) trans. by Charles Williamos<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> of <i>L'art de fabriquer le salin et la potasse</i></li>
<li>(with Pierre-Simon Laplace) <i>Memoir on Heat: Read to the Royal Academy of Sciences, 28 June 1783, by Messrs. Lavoisier &amp; De La Place of the same Academy.</i> (New York: Neale Watson Academic Publications, 1982) trans. by Henry Guerlac of <i>Mémoire sur la chaleur</i></li>
<li><i><a class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/essaysoneffects00henrgoog" rel="nofollow">Essays, on the Effects Produced by Various Processes On Atmospheric Air; With A Particular View To An Investigation Of The Constitution Of Acids</a></i>, trans. Thomas Henry (London: Warrington, 1783) collects these essays:</li></ul>
<ol><li>"Experiments on the Respiration of Animals, and on the Changes effected on the Air in passing through their Lungs." (Read to the Académie des Sciences, 3 May 1777)</li>
<li>"On the Combustion of Candles in Atmospheric Air and in Dephlogistated Air." (Communicated to the Académie des Sciences, 1777)</li>
<li>"On the Combustion of Kunckel's Phosphorus."</li>
<li>"On the Existence of Air in the Nitrous Acid, and on the Means of decomposing and recomposing that Acid."</li>
<li>"On the Solution of Mercury in Vitriolic Acid."</li>
<li>"Experiments on the Combustion of Alum with Phlogistic Substances, and on the Changes effected on Air in which the Pyrophorus was burned."</li>
<li>"On the Vitriolisation of Martial Pyrites."</li>
<li>"General Considerations on the Nature of Acids, and on the Principles of which they are composed."</li>
<li>"On the Combination of the Matter of Fire with Evaporable Fluids; and on the Formation of Elastic Aëriform Fluids."</li></ol>
<ul><li>“Reflections on Phlogiston”, translation by Nicholas W. Best of “Réflexions sur le phlogistique, pour servir de suite à la théorie de la combustion et de la calcination” (read to the Académie Royale des Sciences over two nights, 28 June and 13 July 1783). Published in two parts:</li></ul>

<li id="cite_note-cnrs-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-cnrs_4-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-cnrs_4-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="languageicon">(in French)</span> <a class="external text" href="http://www.cnrs.fr/cw/dossiers/doslavoisier/contenu/alternative/alter2_textes.html" rel="nofollow">Lavoisier, le parcours d'un scientifique révolutionnaire</a> CNRS (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Centre_National_de_la_Recherche_Scientifique" title="Centre National de la Recherche Scientifique">Centre National de la Recherche Scientifique</a>)</span>

<li id="cite_note-Schwinger-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Schwinger_5-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFSchwinger1986"><a href="/wiki/Julian_Schwinger" title="Julian Schwinger">Schwinger, Julian</a> (1986). <a class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/einsteinslegacyu00schw/page/93" rel="nofollow"><i>Einstein's Legacy</i></a>. New York: Scientific American Library. p. <a class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/einsteinslegacyu00schw/page/93" rel="nofollow">93</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-7167-5011-6" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-7167-5011-6"><bdi>978-0-7167-5011-6</bdi></a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Einstein%27s+Legacy&amp;rft.place=New+York&amp;rft.pages=93&amp;rft.pub=Scientific+American+Library&amp;rft.date=1986&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-7167-5011-6&amp;rft.aulast=Schwinger&amp;rft.aufirst=Julian&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Farchive.org%2Fdetails%2Feinsteinslegacyu00schw%2Fpage%2F93&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAntoine+Lavoisier"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-6">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In his table of the elements, Lavoisier listed five "salifiable earths" (i.e., ores that could be made to react with acids to produce salts (<i>salis</i> = salt, in Latin)): <i>chaux</i> (calcium oxide), <i>magnésie</i> (magnesia, magnesium oxide), <i>baryte</i> (barium sulfate), <i>alumine</i> (alumina, aluminum oxide), and <i>silice</i> (silica, silicon dioxide). About these "elements", Lavoisier speculates:  "We are probably only acquainted as yet with a part of the metallic substances existing in nature, as all those which have a stronger affinity to oxygen than carbon possesses, are incapable, hitherto, of being reduced to a metallic state, and consequently, being only presented to our observation under the form of oxyds, are confounded with earths. It is extremely probable that barytes, which we have just now arranged with earths, is in this situation; for in many experiments it exhibits properties nearly approaching to those of metallic bodies. It is even possible that all the substances we call earths may be only metallic oxyds, irreducible by any hitherto known process." – from <a class="extiw" href="//archive.org/details/elementschemist00kerrgoog/page/n217" title="iarchive:elementschemist00kerrgoog/page/n217">p. 218</a> of:   Lavoisier with Robert Kerr, trans., <i>Elements of Chemistry</i>, ..., 4th ed. (Edinburgh, Scotland: William Creech, 1799).  (The original passage appears in: Lavoisier, <i>Traité Élémentaire de Chimie</i>, ...  (Paris, France: Cuchet, 1789), vol. 1, <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=hZch3yOrayUC&amp;pg=PA174" rel="nofollow">p. 174</a>.)</span>
</li>

Alfred A Knopf. p. 73.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Citizens%3A+A+Chronicle+of+the+French+Revolution&amp;rft.pages=73&amp;rft.pub=Alfred+A+Knopf&amp;rft.date=1989&amp;rft.aulast=Schama&amp;rft.aufirst=Simon&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAntoine+Lavoisier"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-29"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-29">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation web cs1" id="CITEREFO'ConnorRobertson,_E.F.2006">O'Connor, J.J.; Robertson, E.F. (26 September 2006). <a class="external text" href="http://www-groups.dcs.st-and.ac.uk/~history/Biographies/Lagrange.html" rel="nofollow">"Joseph-Louis Lagrange"</a>. <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20060502072418/http://www-groups.dcs.st-and.ac.uk/~history/Biographies/Lagrange.html" rel="nofollow">Archived</a> from the original on 2 May 2006<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">20 April</span> 2006</span>. <q>In September 1793 a law was passed ordering the arrest of all foreigners born in enemy countries and all their property to be confiscated. Lavoisier intervened on behalf of Lagrange, who certainly fell under the terms of the law. On 8 May 1794, after a trial that lasted less than a day, a revolutionary tribunal condemned Lavoisier and 27 others to death. Lagrange said on the death of Lavoisier, who was guillotined on the afternoon of the day of his trial</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Joseph-Louis+Lagrange&amp;rft.date=2006-09-26&amp;rft.aulast=O%27Connor&amp;rft.aufirst=J.J.&amp;rft.au=Robertson%2C+E.F.&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww-groups.dcs.st-and.ac.uk%2F~history%2FBiographies%2FLagrange.html&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAntoine+Lavoisier"></span></span>
